Implementation: GeoTerrainBiasFunction (DensityFunction.SimpleFunction wrapping only finalDensity #12), TerrainRouterWrapping (shared install-gate helper), RandomStateAccessor + RandomStateRouterTerrainMixin (ChunkMap-constructor-TAIL interception, chosen over the design's primary RandomState-constructor target because that site has no reliable positive globe check in scope), 3 new LatitudeV2Flags all defaulting to a true no-op. Mechanical proof harness (TerrainProofHarness) initially reported "34/34 PASS" across Classic/Mercator, but its own structural check (a real NoiseChunk build, not just direct compute()) caught a real defect first: DensityFunction.SimpleFunction's default mapChildren ("return this") hid the wrapped delegate from NoiseChunk's cache/interpolation-substitution visitor, breaking installed-but-strength=0 byte-identity in structure (not value) -- fixed by overriding mapChildren to recurse via the visitor (closes design residual R5). Also surfaced a K-scaling finding: strength=1.0 with K=0.25 on vanilla density produced a floating landmass Y~106-320 (design R4, live-pass calibration concern). A subsequent 6-lens sweeper audit (workflow wf_2de5fa57-e76, 32 agents) found the "34/34 PASS" claim was NOT trustworthy (26 raw findings, 23 confirmed on independent verification -- an unusually high rate) and one CRITICAL defect the mechanical proof never exercised: TerrainRouterWrapping's gate checked only the GEO_V2_ENABLED boolean as proof GeoAuthority's land/ocean field was live, but LatitudeBiomes.rebuildGeoAuthority() only builds a real GeoAuthorityProvider when seed != 0 && zRadius > 0 -- on a seed-0 world the flag says "on" but the provider silently stays the NEUTRAL no-op (land01=0.0 everywhere), so the wrapper would have pushed the ENTIRE WORLD downward (100%-ocean bias); recorded as LESSONS L17. Separately, the harness's own non-globe/globe-gate-isolation leg crashed on an empty-string-forwarded property (Gradle vmArg forwarding sends "" not "absent" for an unpassed knob) and, independently, booted an actually-armed globe world while labeling itself excluded, so that leg never validly ran. All HIGH/MEDIUM findings fixed for real (critical fix: gate on `geoProviderForTerrain() instanceof GeoAuthorityProvider`, refusing install regardless of the flag if the provider is still NoOp; harness now records a definitive installResult/wrapperInstalled/geoProviderClass per run and hard-fails if a leg's actual world classification doesn't match what it claims); LOW findings fixed or disposed with a stated reason. Design doc updated with a residual R7 (absolute-Y alpine snow-line can put a cold snow cap on a lifted subtropical peak -- the "cold biome in a warm latitude" failure class this project watches for) and an addendum recording the ChunkMap-relocation gate as final, not a fallback | worldgen | `JAVA_HOME=<temurin-25> ./gradlew compileJava test` (BUILD SUCCESSFUL, 0 failures) independently re-run by the coordinator after each commit, not just trusted from agent summaries; | 20260706-arid-savanna-boundary-fray | 2026-07-06 | worldgen | Peetsa found a visually-wrong narrow, dead-straight arid/savanna strip cutting across a mountain range (screenshots at seed 0, geoV2.enabled + terrainV2.enabled/strength=0.05, Mercator regular). | 20260708-ui-pass-round3-fixes | 2026-07-08 | rendering | TEST 30 UI pass round 3: three bugs from Peetsa's screen recording, reviewed frame-by-frame at native resolution before any fix, three independent root causes, all fixed. (1) Atlas position "bouncing" across World Size Small/Regular/Large/Ginormous ("the word ATLAS, everything down"): computeSizeLabelBottom() reserved vertical space using only the CURRENTLY SELECTED size's wrapped description line count, so leftPreviewTopY (driving both the ATLAS heading and the map's top) moved whenever a different size's description text happened to wrap to a different number of lines — previewHeight itself never varied, this was the whole section sliding, not the map resizing. FIX: reserve the worst-case line count across all six SIZE_DESCRIPTIONS (same reserved-width pattern as the compass HUD), so the section's position is size-invariant; short descriptions leave trailing blank space instead. (2) Tape look + Attach to Hotbar rendering off-screen in the HUD Studio preview ONLY (correct live in-game): the Studio-preview render call site (CompassHud.renderInternal's forceVisible branch) fed computeAnalogBounds()'s content-true hitbox y into renderAnalogAt, which expects the DIAL-BOX top-left (the contract the live path satisfies via computeAnalogDialPos) — round 2's box-vs-content adjustment (needed because Tape's drawn content is shorter than its diameter box) got applied a SECOND time on top of an already-adjusted value, doubling the downward offset. Every other look has content==box (adjustment is a no-op), which is exactly why only Tape showed the bug. FIX: the Studio-preview call site now computes the actual dial-box position the same way the live path does; the now-unreachable computePreviewBounds() was deleted rather than left as dead code. (3) Inner Transparency checkerboard aid "locked on" the instant the slider is touched, never disappearing: transparencyAdjustActive() (round 2) gated on slider.isFocused(), and vanilla widget focus is STICKY — it persists past mouseUp until a DIFFERENT widget takes focus, so one click-drag latched the checkerboard on for the rest of the Studio session (tab-switching happened to "fix" it only because that rebuilds every widget from scratch). FIX: isFocused() dropped entirely; FloatSlider (shared by Analog Size and Inner Transparency) now tracks its own click-to-release lifecycle explicitly via overridden onClick/onRelease (isDragging()), which cannot get stuck. | 20260709-ui-pass-round10-random-sweep | 2026-07-09 | rendering | Create-screen round 10: Peetsa wanted the Random spawn zone to feel special on the atlas -- start colored in the middle, bands "strobe/cycle outward in opposing directions," a colorful double scroll. Implemented in LatitudePlanisphereRenderer.renderCompact for the selectedBand==null (Random) case ONLY: a Gaussian glow pulse starts at the equator and travels outward through the latitude bands to the poles; because every band is drawn mirrored north+south, one advancing pulse reads as two lit regions moving APART = the double scroll in opposing directions. As the pulse passes a band, that band brightens in its OWN native climate color and turns nearly opaque (the same ~1.30x brighten + high alpha the selected band uses), settling back to the normal muted 0x86 wash away from the front. A gold crest line rides the pulse front (mirrored N+S, sine-eased alpha so it doesn't blink at the loop seam), echoing the selected-zone gold edge. frontDeg runs past the pole (POLE_FADE_DEG=108) so the polar band fully fades before the loop restarts at the equator -- matching "initially colored in the middle, cycle outward." Wall-clock driven (System.currentTimeMillis % RANDOM_SWEEP_PERIOD_MS, same idiom as the Aurora compass theme; create screen redraws every frame). 3 cosmetic tuning constants: RANDOM_SWEEP_PERIOD_MS=3200 (one equator->pole loop), RANDOM_SWEEP_SIGMA_DEG=16 (how many bands lit at once), POLE_FADE_DEG=108. Non-Random rendering is BYTE-IDENTICAL -- selected-band pop, muted others, and static gold outline all untouched; the animation is entirely inside the selectedBand==null branch. | 20260708-ui-pass-round8-fixes | 2026-07-08 | rendering | Create-screen round 8: Peetsa reported the atlas preview clips off the panel at Tiny world size when Classic (1:1 square) world shape is selected, and Itty Bitty still looks very large -- asked to shrink the 1:1 rendering only, leave 2:1 Mercator untouched. ROOT CAUSE: renderPlanispherePreview's radius fit-budget computes a widthDivisor (2.0*MERCATOR_ASPECT=4.0 for Mercator vs 2.0 for Classic, reflecting that a Mercator globe is 2x as wide as tall for the same radius) -- correct in principle, but for the SAME panel this makes Classic's width-derived radius budget come out roughly DOUBLE Mercator's, which in practice makes Classic almost always height-bound (maxRadiusByHeight, identical for both shapes, wins the min() against the now-generous maxRadiusByWidth). Consequence: previewDiscFill's per-world-size grading (0.70 Itty Bitty ramping to 0.99 Ginormous) barely mattered for Classic since it was already pinned near the height ceiling regardless of size (too large at every size, worst at Itty Bitty since 0.70 of an already-oversized height budget still reads big), and with so little width headroom actually spent there was little margin left once the real composition math (label width/padding/frame border, applied in the existing fit-shrink loop) was subtracted, clipping at Tiny specifically. Mercator never had this problem since its stricter 4.0 divisor keeps it reliably width-bound, where previewDiscFill has real room to operate. FIX: new CLASSIC_ATLAS_SCALE constant, applied to the computed radius ONLY when shape != MERCATOR, inserted after the existing shared width/height-budget + disc-fill math and before the fit-shrink loop runs -- Mercator's code path reads nothing new and stays byte-identical. FIRST TRY 0.62f overshot: Peetsa reported Ginormous now read about like Small/Regular and Itty Bitty wasn't much smaller either -- root cause, the multiplier scales every size down by the SAME fraction so it shrinks the ABSOLUTE pixel gap between sizes right along with the overall size, compressing the whole size range into a visually narrow band. RAISED to 0.82f (happy medium between the original 1.0 that clipped and the 0.62 that bunched sizes together) | rendering | compileJava + pure-JVM suite (cleanTest test) green; ./gradlew clean build green | pass | - | /Users/joolmac/CascadeProjects/Latitude-2.0-26.2-pivot/docs/binder/ui-pass-round8-fixes-20260708.md | TEST 39.jar staged SHA 84f6c803da4297d812831722d58c3b8122c78b7df8a14d014e8eaf62b7ec558a verified source↔staged, supersedes TEST 38.jar (which superseded TEST 37.jar [0.62 attempt] and TEST 36.jar; same worldgen args, C-3 untouched); Peetsa re-checks live: cycle all 6 world sizes on Classic (no clipping, visibly distinct sizes Itty Bitty->Ginormous, not too big) and confirm Mercator's atlas is visually unchanged from TEST 36 at the same sizes | active | - |

| 20260708-ui-pass-round6-fixes | 2026-07-08 | rendering | HUD Studio round 6: restored "opacity" wording (Peetsa: not jargon) in the 3 tooltips round 5 changed to "see-through" (Inner Transparency, digital Transparency, Text Opacity) while keeping the plain comma-list phrasing elsewhere. REAL BUG FOUND AND FIXED: "after you click on a button and go back and hover over it, the tooltip is gone and will not come back." Decompiled the 26.2 CycleButton class (javap on the loom-cached minecraft-merged.jar) and found the exact mechanism: CycleButton has its OWN internal tooltip system -- a private tooltipSupplier field consulted by a private updateTooltip() that vanilla calls AUTOMATICALLY on every value change (every click), with literally no null-check: this.setTooltip(this.tooltipSupplier.apply(this.value)). This codebase attaches every Studio tooltip externally via a shared tooltip(widget,text) helper calling AbstractWidget.setTooltip(...) directly after the CycleButton.Builder chain finishes -- the builder's own .withTooltip(...) is never called anywhere in this file, so tooltipSupplier sits at its no-op default (returns null) for all ~30 CycleButton instances in the Studio (Compass Style, Direction Format, Compass Look, Color Scheme, Attach to Hotbar, Title Case, Show HUD, etc). The FIRST click on ANY of them fires updateTooltip(), which overwrites the externally-set tooltip with null -- PERMANENTLY, since WidgetTooltipHolder.refreshTooltipForNextRenderPass's first line is "if (tooltip == null) return" -- hovering afterward can never bring it back because the Tooltip OBJECT itself is gone, not merely hidden. (Buttons whose onValueChange calls this.init() -- Compass Style, Compass Look -- appeared to "recover" only because init() rebuilds a fresh widget instance and reattaches the tooltip from scratch; plain toggles that don't reinit stayed broken for the rest of the session, matching Peetsa's exact report.) FIX: the shared tooltip() helper now detects CycleButton instances and patches tooltipSupplier via reflection (no public setter exists post-construction; the builder-time alternative would mean editing all ~30 call sites instead of the one shared helper) to a constant supplier always returning the SAME Tooltip object -- correct because every Studio tooltip is static text that doesn't vary with the button's current value. Reflection failure (future field rename) degrades gracefully to the old (buggy-after-one-click) behavior rather than throwing. Also confirmed: the Title Case tooltip already lists Normal correctly from the prior same-day correction commit -- no further change needed | rendering | compileJava + pure-JVM suite (cleanTest) green; root cause confirmed via javap bytecode disassembly of CycleButton.updateTooltip() and WidgetTooltipHolder.refreshTooltipForNextRenderPass() from the actual 26.2 minecraft-merged.jar, not guesswork | pass | - | /Users/joolmac/CascadeProjects/Latitude-2.0-26.2-pivot/docs/binder/ui-pass-round6-fixes-20260708.md | TEST 34.jar staged SHA f656dc5bed9031ea9414435ee1d24e7dd9a0d0edc0a62b776915c582241a1c36 verified source↔staged, supersedes TEST 33.jar (same worldgen args, C-3 untouched); Peetsa re-checks live: click a CycleButton, move mouse off and back, tooltip should reappear -- test both a plain toggle and a multi-value cycle | active | - |

## Topic note
- topic `worldgen`: next entry should be recorded from `tmp/*` proof runs that changed biome/world behavior.
- topic `rendering`: use this registry whenever rendering/protocol/overlay invariants are validated.
- topic `compatibility`: record API migration, datapack, and third-party compatibility investigations.
- topic `release`: record release gate and checklist completion evidence.
- topic `migration`: record client migration or API compatibility status snapshots.
- topic `bug blaster`: use `trigger: BugBlaster: <issue-or-topic>` with the underlying affected scope.

## Supersession procedure
- If a prior row is replaced, add a new row with the same scope and a `supersedes` value.
- Old row status must be updated to `superseded` in a follow-up entry.
- Keep historical rows for auditability.
